*Remark 4.2* (On the adversary outputting the set of insiders). In our model, the adversary outputs the sets of insiders Isk and Ipd, along with the decoder *D*. This models the following scenario in the real world:

If a set of colluders decides to sell a decoder to a set of one or more insiders, we argue that at least the set of insiders themselves must know who the insiders are to make the decoder work (i.e., if they do not know whose keys to input into the decoder to make it work, it is essentially useless and has no decryption advantage). Since they are the ones who "blow the whistle" and forward the decoder to the tracer, they forward the set of insiders together with the decoder.

Another way of seeing this is as follows: If any set of less than *t* committee members can make a decoder work (such that it has a noticeable decryption advantage) by inputting their secret keys or partial decryptions, then, by definition, they are a valid set of insiders and could blow the whistle by forwarding the decoder to the tracer. A similar logic was used in a recent work [\[40\]](#page-65-10) in the collusion-resilient secret sharing setting, where decoders come with an "instruction manual" (i.e., the set of parties from which additional shares are required).

*Remark 4.3* (Requiring insiders' secret keys is justified). We also argue that it is *justified* in practice to require insiders' secret keys for tracing, since insiders already act as whistleblowers. Hence, they have a vested interest in tracing to succeed, so they can be assumed to forward their secret keys to the tracer along with the decoder. Alternatively, one could give the tracer the authority to force committee members to decommit their secret keys once a good decoder is found, since secrecy is broken at this point anyway.[5](#page-17-1)

*Remark 4.4* (Tracing can use partial insiders' secret keys). We note that it is not strictly necessary to require that the tracer also gets access to the *partial insiders'* secret keys. In fact, our maximally partial-insider resilient construction in Section [10](#page-43-0) allows the tracer to simulate partial decryptions to the decoder, provided he knows the randomness used to generate the ciphertext, and thus, it does not need partial insiders' secret keys for tracing.

Nevertheless, in this work, we treat partial insiders as a relaxation of full insiders, which we consider the more natural perspective. To prove that full-insider resilience generically implies partial-insider resilience, the tracer must be given access to partial insiders' secret keys. This is because we proved that full insiders' secret keys are *necessary* for tracing. Consequently, if resilience against full insiders is to imply resilience against an equal number of partial insiders, the tracer must retain access to the partial insiders' secret keys. Indeed, resilience against full insiders may inherently rely on the tracer's access to the corresponding secret keys. Removing this information in the partial-insider setting could eliminate essential information for tracing to succeed.

*Remark 4.5* (On public tracing). In this paper, we work in the *private tracing* setting, where tracing relies on a secret tracing key, as most threshold traitor tracing schemes in the literature support only

<span id="page-17-1"></span><sup>5</sup>This could be realized, e.g., by forcing committee members to lock a stake that is slashed upon non-compliance.

{18}------------------------------------------------

<span id="page-18-2"></span>private tracing [12, 3, 21, 28]. Insider resilience, however, is equally relevant in a public tracing setting, where the tracing key is public. In fact, public threshold tracing schemes such as [24] and [23] exhibit exactly the *unlocking mechanism* that makes threshold traitor tracing schemes vulnerable to insiders.

Our definition can be straightforwardly amended to support public tracing by granting the adversary access to the tracing key tk. Moreover, none of our compilers inherently rely on the fact that the tracing key is kept secret, and can be securely instantiated with public tracing schemes, yielding public tracing schemes as a result.

Finally, we define the term *limitless*, referring to TT-KEMs that can trace decoders with arbitrary but noticeable decryption advantage.

**Definition 4.6** (Limitless). We say that a TT-KEM is *limitless*, if Definition 4.1 applies for any  $\varepsilon \in 1/\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)$  and the KGen algorithm does not rely on  $\varepsilon$ .

In [51], Zhandry showed how to compile any *limited* traitor tracing scheme to a *limitless* scheme. This result was extended in [28] to the traceable threshold encryption setting. We further extend Zhandry's limit elimination compiler to support multi-traitor tracing and insiders in Appendix B.

## <span id="page-18-0"></span>4.1 Full Insider Tracing without Secret Keys is Impossible

In this section, we show that it is necessary for the tracer to obtain secret keys of full insiders  $\{sk_i\}_{i\in\mathcal{I}_{sk}}$ . More formally, we show that there cannot exist a traceable threshold encryption scheme that is both traceable against at least 1 full insider without access to the secret keys, and semantically secure against the tracer.

<span id="page-18-1"></span>**Theorem 4.7** There does not exist a TT-KEM that is both 1-traceable against 1 full insider without access to the full insider's secret key and semantically secure.

For simplicity, we prove the theorem for a perfect TT-KEM, i.e., a TT-KEM with perfect correctness and no ramp.

Proof of Theorem 4.7. We prove the theorem by assuming that  $\Pi$  is a perfect TT-KEM that is 1-traceable against 1 full insider. Then we construct an adversary  $\mathcal{A}$  against 1-traceability that always corrupts t-1 parties, designates one additional party  $p_{\mathsf{ins}}$  as full insider, and produces a good decoder, and thus, by assumption, the decoder it produces must be traced successfully with overwhelming probability. On any given input  $(k, c, \mathsf{sk}_{p_{\mathsf{ins}}})$ , the decoder produced by  $\mathcal{A}$  first checks whether the secret key of the full insider is "valid" by checking whether it can be used to decrypt a new random ciphertext (alongside the traitors' secret keys). If this check fails, i.e., the secret key is invalid, the decoder always outputs 0 instead.

Then, we argue as follows: First, a decoder that *always* outputs 0 cannot be traced, except with negligible probability due to unframability. Hence, the tracer must make at least one query to the decoder, where the given secret key passes the validity test.

Thus, we can use  $\mathcal{A}$  to break semantic security of  $\Pi$  by internally running the tracer on D using the tracing key (which is known to the adversary in the semantic security game). Assuming the tracer makes a maximum of  $Q \in \mathsf{poly}(\lambda)$  queries to D,  $\mathcal{A}$  picks a random query to embed the IND-CPA challenge  $(k^*, c^*)$  into the validity check, and outputs the result to its challenger.  $\mathcal{A}$  has probability 1/Q to hit the valid query by the tracer, in which case it will win the semantic security game. We next formalize this approach.

Fix an arbitrary  $\varepsilon \in (0, 1/2]$ . Let  $\mathcal{A}$  be the following PPT adversary against Game-Tr<sub> $\Pi$ </sub>:  $\mathcal{A}$  initially corrupts t-1 random parties  $\mathcal{T} = \{p_1, \dots, p_{t-1}\}$  as traitors and designates another random party  $p_{\mathsf{ins}}$  as full insider. Then,  $\mathcal{A}$  constructs a decoder D as follows: On input  $(k, c, \mathsf{sk}_{p_{\mathsf{ins}}})$ , the decoder samples  $(k', c') \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathsf{Enc}(\mathsf{pk})$  and computes partial decryptions  $d_i \leftarrow \mathsf{PDec}(\mathsf{sk}, c)$  for all traitors  $i \in \mathcal{T}$ . Then it computes a partial decryption on behalf of the insider:  $d_{p_{\mathsf{ins}}} \leftarrow \mathsf{PDec}(\mathsf{sk}_{p_{\mathsf{ins}}}, c)$ . Next, the decoder checks whether

 $\mathsf{valid} \coloneqq \left[k' \stackrel{?}{=} \mathsf{Combine}\Big(\mathsf{pk}, \mathcal{T} \cup \{p_\mathsf{ins}\}, \{d_i\}_{i \in \mathcal{T} \cup \{p_\mathsf{ins}\}}, c\Big)\right].$ 

Denote with valid the event that the above check succeeds. If valid = 1, behave like a good decoder: Decrypt c using the traitors' secret keys alongside  $\mathsf{sk}_{p_\mathsf{ins}}$ , output 0 if the resulting key is equal to k and 1 otherwise. Else, if valid = 0, always output 0, essentially acting like the Dummy decoder. Finally,  $\mathcal{A}$  outputs  $(D, \mathcal{I}_\mathsf{sk} \coloneqq \{p_\mathsf{ins}\})$  to the Game-Tr challenger.

We next prove two claims that will allow us to show that A can be used to break semantic security.

{19}------------------------------------------------

<span id="page-19-2"></span>Claim 4.8 It holds that  $Pr[GoodDec_A] = 1$ .

Proof of Claim 4.8. First, observe that  $\sigma=1=|\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}}|$ , hence none of the assertions in Game-Tr fails, and GoodDec is not set to 0 by default. Due to perfect correctness of  $\Pi$ , it must hold that whenever D is queried with a valid secret key  $\mathsf{sk}_{p_{\mathsf{ins}}}$ , then  $\mathsf{valid}=1$ , and thus, again by perfect correctness, D guesses correctly whether k is real or random. Hence, it holds that  $P(D)=1\geq 1/2+\varepsilon$  for any  $\varepsilon\in(0,1/2]$ .

<span id="page-19-3"></span>Claim 4.9 Let  $Q \in \mathsf{poly}(\lambda)$  be an upper bound on the number of queries to the decoder made by the Trace algorithm. When running  $\mathsf{Trace}^D(\mathsf{pk},\mathsf{tk},\varepsilon,\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}})$ , it holds that  $\mathsf{valid}=1$  for at least one query made to D, except with negligible probability.

Proof of Claim 4.9. We prove the claim by contradiction. Let  $\gamma$  be the probability that  $\mathsf{valid} = 0$  across all of the queries made by  $\mathsf{Trace}^D$ , and assume that  $\gamma$  is non-negligible. Observe that, if no valid queries are made, then D always outputs 0, and thus acts like a dummy decoder. Also, note that by Claim 4.9 and the assumption that  $\Pi$  is traceable, it must hold that  $\mathsf{Pr}[\mathsf{GoodTr}_{\mathcal{A}}] \geq 1 - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$  for a negligible function  $\mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$ , which implies that

$$\Pr\left[ \begin{aligned} \operatorname{Trace}^D(\mathsf{pk},\mathsf{tk},\varepsilon,\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}}) \neq \emptyset \colon & \begin{pmatrix} \mathsf{pk}, \{\mathsf{sk}_i\}_{i \in [n]},\mathsf{tk} \end{pmatrix} \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathsf{KGen}(1^\lambda,n,t,\varepsilon) \\ \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}} \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \binom{[n]}{1}; & \mathcal{T} \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \binom{[n] \backslash \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}}}{t-1} \end{pmatrix} \right] \geq 1 - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda). \end{aligned}$$

Together with the assumption that D acts like a dummy decoder with probability  $\gamma$ , we can conclude that

$$\Pr\left[\mathsf{Trace}^{\mathsf{Dummy}}(\mathsf{pk},\mathsf{tk},\varepsilon,\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}}) \neq \emptyset \colon \begin{array}{c} \left(\mathsf{pk}, \left\{\mathsf{sk}_i\right\}_{i \in [n]},\mathsf{tk}\right) \xleftarrow{\$} \mathsf{KGen}(1^{\lambda}, n, t, \varepsilon) \\ \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}} \xleftarrow{\$} \binom{[n]}{1} \end{array} \right] \geq \gamma - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda),$$

which is a contradiction with unframability of  $\Pi$ . To see this, consider an adversary  $\mathcal{B}$  that corrupts no party and outputs the dummy decoder Dummy alongside a random full insider. Then  $\Pr[\mathsf{BadTr}_{\mathcal{B}}] \geq \gamma - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$ , which we initially assumed to be non-negligible.

Equipped with Claims 4.8 and 4.9, we now show that we can construct a successful adversary  $\mathcal{B}$  against Game-IND-CPA of  $\Pi$ .

First,  $\mathcal{B}$  samples the set  $\mathsf{Cor} \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \binom{[n]}{t-1}$ , forwards it to its challenger, and receives as a response the tuple  $(\mathsf{pk}, \mathsf{tk}, \{\mathsf{sk}_i\}_{i \in \mathsf{Cor}}, k^*, c^*)$ . Then,  $\mathcal{B}$  samples  $\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}} \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \binom{[n] \setminus \mathsf{Cor}}{1}$ , and constructs the decoder D for  $\mathcal{T} \coloneqq \mathsf{Cor}$  and  $\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}}$ . Finally,  $\mathcal{B}$  chooses a random  $q \in Q$  and, using  $\mathsf{tk}$ , runs  $\mathsf{Trace}^D(\mathsf{pk}, \mathsf{tk}, \varepsilon, \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}})$ , simulating the behavior of D perfectly up until the q-th query. In the q-th query,  $\mathcal{B}$  embeds the IND-CPA challenge  $(k^*, c^*)$  into the validity check:  $\mathcal{B}$  computes  $d_i \leftarrow \mathsf{PDec}(\mathsf{sk}_i, c^*)$  for all  $i \in \mathcal{T}$  as well as  $d_{p_{\mathsf{ins}}} \leftarrow \mathsf{PDec}(\mathsf{sk}_{p_{\mathsf{ins}}}, c^*)$ , where  $\mathsf{sk}_{p_{\mathsf{ins}}}$  is parsed from the input of the q-th query to D. Finally,  $\mathcal{B}$  outputs 0 if  $k^* = \mathsf{Combine}(\mathsf{pk}, \mathcal{T} \cup \{p_{\mathsf{ins}}\}, \{d_i\}_{i \in \mathcal{T} \cup \{p_{\mathsf{ins}}\}}, c^*)$ , indicating that the challenge key  $k^*$  is real, and 1 otherwise. If tracing issues less than q queries,  $\mathcal{B}$  instead outputs a random bit.

Analysis. Observe that if tracing issues at least one query such that valid = 1, then  $\mathcal{B}$  guesses this query with probability at least 1/Q. Applying Claim 4.9, we can conclude that

$$\Pr\left[\mathsf{Game\text{-}IND\text{-}CPA}_{\mathcal{B}}(1^{\lambda},n,t,\varepsilon) = 1\right] \geq \frac{1}{2} + \frac{1 - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)}{Q},$$

and thus  $\mathcal B$  breaks IND-CPA security with a non-negligible advantage.

# <span id="page-19-0"></span>5 Insider Resilience from Multi-Traitor Tracing

Next, we formalize our approach to traceability against insider collusion by utilizing schemes that enable  $tracing\ multiple\ traitors$ . We do so in two steps: First, we show that one can accept identifying  $x\ fewer$  traitors as a trade-off to gain resilience against  $x\ more\ full\ insiders$  (Theorem 5.2). Second, we show that one can accept resilience against  $y\ fewer\ full\ insiders$ , to achieve resilience against  $y\ more\ partial\ insiders$  (Theorem 5.3). The following corollary summarizes this result.

<span id="page-19-1"></span>Corollary 5.1 Any TT-KEM that is  $\tau$ -traceable against  $(\sigma, \rho)$ -insiders is also  $(\tau - x)$ -traceable against  $(\sigma + x - y, \rho + y)$ -insiders for all  $x, y \in \mathbb{N}$  with  $0 \le x < \tau$  and  $0 \le y \le \sigma + x$ .

{20}------------------------------------------------

In particular, Corollary 5.1 implies that any  $\tau$ -traceable scheme without insider resilience is also 1-traceable against  $(\sigma, \rho)$ -insiders, provided that  $\sigma + \rho < \tau$ . Importantly, we show that one does not have to fix this tradeoff at the time of instantiation: The same scheme is traceable against all supported trade-offs among  $\tau$ ,  $\sigma$ , and  $\rho$  at the same time.

#### <span id="page-20-0"></span>5.1 Multi-Traitor to Full Insiders

We next show the first step, i.e., trading traitors found for full insiders. Let  $\Pi$  be a TT-KEM that is  $\tau$ -traceable against  $(\sigma, \rho)$ -insiders with  $\tau > 1$ . Our compiler allows us to tolerate up to  $\tau - 1$  additional full insiders by hardcoding their secret keys into the decoder during tracing, and removing the additional full insiders from the set of identified traitors at the end. More generally, we show that such a scheme is also  $(\tau - x)$ -traceable against  $(\sigma + x, \rho)$  for all  $0 \le x < \tau$ . We denote  $\tau' = \tau - x$  and  $\sigma' = \sigma + x$ .

<span id="page-20-3"></span>**Construction 1** (Mult-Traitor to Full Insiders). Let  $\Pi$  be a TT-KEM that is  $\tau$ -traceable against  $(\sigma, \rho)$ -insiders. We construct  $\Pi'$  which is identical to  $\Pi$  except for a modification to the Trace algorithm:  $\Pi'$ . Trace  $\Pi'$  (pk, tk,  $\varepsilon$ ,  $\mathcal{I}_{sk}'$ ,  $\mathcal{I}_{pd}'$ , {sk $_i$ } $_{i \in \mathcal{I}_{sk}' \cup \mathcal{I}_{pd}'}$ ): If  $|\mathcal{I}_{sk}'| \geq \tau + \sigma$ , abort and output  $\mathcal{T}' = \emptyset$ . Otherwise, proceed with the following steps:

- Sample the set  $\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}}$  as an arbitrary subset of  $\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}}'$  of size  $\min(\sigma, |\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}}'|)$ , i.e.,  $\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}} \subseteq \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}}'$  and  $|\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}}| = \min(\sigma, |\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}}'|)$ . Also, let the set of full insiders for  $\Pi'$  that are not insiders for  $\Pi$  be  $\mathcal{N}_{\mathsf{sk}} \leftarrow \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}}' \setminus \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}}$ , and let  $\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}} \leftarrow \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}}'$ .
- Construct a decoder D for  $\Pi$ . On input  $(c, k, \{\overline{\mathsf{sk}_i}\}_{i \in \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}}}, \{d_i\}_{i \in \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}}})$ , the decoder D outputs  $D'(c, k, \{\overline{\mathsf{sk}_i}\}_{i \in \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}}}) \cup \{\mathsf{sk}_i\}_{i \in \mathcal{N}_{\mathsf{sk}}}, \{d_i\}_{i \in \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}}})$ .
- Run  $\mathcal{T}'_{\mathsf{ins}} \overset{\hspace{0.1em}\mathsf{\scriptscriptstyle\$}}{\leftarrow} \Pi.\mathsf{Trace}^D(\mathsf{pk},\mathsf{tk},\varepsilon,\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}},\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}},\{\mathsf{sk}_i\}_{i\in\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}}\cup\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}}}), \text{ output } \mathcal{T}'\leftarrow\mathcal{T}'_{\mathsf{ins}}\setminus\mathcal{N}_{\mathsf{sk}}.$

<span id="page-20-1"></span>**Theorem 5.2** If  $\Pi$  is  $\tau$ -traceable against  $(\sigma, \rho)$ -insiders, then Construction 1 is  $(\tau - x)$ -traceable against  $(\sigma + x, \rho)$ -insiders for all  $0 \le x \le \tau$ .

Since the construction does not rely on specifying x ahead of time, Theorem 5.2 implies that the tracing algorithm always returns the maximum number of traitors, i.e., we do not have to limit ourselves to a specific choice of  $\tau'$  and  $\sigma'$  at the time of setup or key generation.

As an example, suppose we instantiate our theorem with a scheme  $\Pi$  where  $\sigma=0$  and  $\tau=t$ . If the tracer gets access to a decoder that does not require full insiders, he will identify  $\tau$  traitors. If, instead, the decoder requires, say, 2 full insiders, it will identify  $\tau-2$  traitors. We address this subtle detail in the following proof.

*Proof of Theorem 5.2.* Fix arbitrary,  $\tau$ ,  $\sigma$ , and  $\rho$  for an arbitrary base scheme  $\Pi$  such that  $0 < \tau \le t$  and  $0 < \tau + \sigma + \rho \le t$  and assume that  $\Pi$  is  $\tau$ -traceable against  $(\sigma, \rho)$ -insiders. Let  $\mathcal{A}$  be any PPT adversary against traceability of  $\Pi'$ .

In the following, we introduce a number of random variables for  $\mathcal{A}$  running in Game-Tr. Denote with  $\mathcal{T}_{\mathcal{A}}$  the random variable capturing the set of traitors corrupted by  $\mathcal{A}$  through its corruption oracle in Game-Tr, and with  $\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}'_{\mathcal{A}}}$  as well as  $\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}'_{\mathcal{A}}}$  the set of full and partial insiders output by  $\mathcal{A}$ . Denote  $\mathcal{I}'_{\mathcal{A}} = \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}'_{\mathcal{A}}} \cup \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}'_{\mathcal{A}}}$ . W.l.o.g., assume that  $\mathcal{I}'_{\mathcal{A}} \subseteq [n]$ ,  $\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}'_{\mathcal{A}}} \cap \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}'_{\mathcal{A}}} = \emptyset$  and  $|\mathcal{I}'_{\mathcal{A}}| < \sigma + \rho + \tau$ . Further, require that  $|\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}'_{\mathcal{A}}}| \le \rho$  as well as  $|\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}'}| < \sigma + \tau$ . Also, denote with D' the decoder produced by  $\mathcal{A}$  and by  $\mathcal{T}'_{\mathcal{A}}$  the set of traitors found when tracing D' against  $\mathcal{I}'_{\mathcal{A}}$ .

We aim to show that there exists a negligible function negl such that

$$\Pr\left[ \overbrace{\mathcal{T}_{\mathcal{A}}' \subseteq \mathcal{T}_{\mathcal{A}} \ \land \ |\mathcal{T}_{\mathcal{A}}'| \geq \tau - \max\left(|\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}_{\mathcal{A}}}'| - \sigma, 0\right)]}^{\mathsf{GoodTr}_{\mathcal{A}} \ \text{for arbitrary } 0 \leq x \leq \tau \right] \geq \Pr[\mathsf{GoodDec}_{\mathcal{A}}] - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda).$$

Intuitively, the above statement expresses the following guarantee: First, we must only find real traitors  $(\mathcal{T}'_{\mathcal{A}} \subseteq \mathcal{T}_{\mathcal{A}})$ , and second, we find at least  $\tau - x$  traitors, whenever the adversary specifies  $\sigma + x$  full insiders. If the adversary should specify less than  $\sigma$  full insiders, we identify  $\tau$  traitors. The above must happen with probability at least  $\Pr[\mathsf{GoodDec}_{\mathcal{A}}] - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$ .

Additionally, we will show that

$$\Pr[\mathsf{BadTr}_{\mathcal{A}}] \leq \mathsf{negl}(\lambda).$$

<span id="page-20-2"></span><sup>&</sup>lt;sup>6</sup>Recall that the decoder D' expects to obtain secret keys on behalf of  $\mathcal{I}_{sk}'$ . By essentially hardcoding the secret keys of  $\mathcal{N}_{sk}$ , D now only expects to obtain secret keys from  $\mathcal{I}_{sk}$ , which is of size at most  $\sigma$  and thus traceable by  $\Pi$ . Trace.

{21}------------------------------------------------

We construct a reduction  $\mathcal{B}$  for  $\tau$ -traceability against  $(\sigma, \rho)$ -inisiders of  $\Pi$  as follows: When  $\mathcal{B}$  receives a public key and public parameters from its challenger, it forwards those to  $\mathcal{A}$ . When  $\mathcal{A}$  issues a corruption query,  $\mathcal{B}$  forwards it to its challenger and returns the resulting secret key to  $\mathcal{A}$ . Similarly,  $\mathcal{B}$  answers queries to  $\mathcal{O}^{\mathsf{PDec-Hon}}$  by querying its own challenger's  $\mathcal{O}^{\mathsf{PDec-Hon}}$  oracle. As a result, when  $\mathcal{A}$  outputs  $(D', \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}'\mathcal{A}}, \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}'\mathcal{A}})$ , it holds that  $\mathcal{T}_{\mathcal{A}} = \mathcal{T}_{\mathcal{B}}$ .

Given a decoder D',  $\mathcal{B}$  must produce a "working" decoder D to return to its  $\Pi$  challenger. However,  $\mathcal{B}$  can pick at most  $\sigma$  secret-key insiders from  $\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}'_{\mathcal{A}}}$  to act as insiders to forward to its own challenger. Hence,  $\mathcal{B}$  must hardcode the remaining keys into D' to produce D. Since  $|\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}'_{\mathcal{A}}}| < \sigma + \tau$ ,  $\mathcal{B}$  hardcodes up to  $\tau - 1$  keys.

To do so,  $\mathcal{B}$  sets  $\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}_{\mathcal{B}}} \leftarrow \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}_{\mathcal{A}}}'$  and samples an arbitrary subset  $\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}_{\mathcal{B}}}$  of  $\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}_{\mathcal{A}}}'$  of size  $\min(|\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}_{\mathcal{A}}}|, \sigma)$  (as mandated by  $\Pi'$ . Trace). Also  $\mathcal{B}$  computes the set  $\mathcal{N}_{\mathsf{sk}} \leftarrow \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}_{\mathcal{A}}} \setminus \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}_{\mathcal{B}}}$ . Note at this point that it must hold that  $|\mathcal{N}_{\mathsf{sk}}| = \max(|\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}_{\mathcal{A}}}'| - \sigma, 0)$ . Next,  $\mathcal{B}$  issues a corruption query to  $\mathcal{O}^{\mathsf{corrupt}}$  to its challenger on behalf of each party in  $\mathcal{N}_{\mathsf{sk}}$ , thereby learning their secret keys. Now it holds that  $\mathcal{T}_{\mathcal{B}} = \mathcal{T}_{\mathcal{A}} \cup \mathcal{N}_{\mathsf{sk}}$ . Set  $\mathcal{I}_{\mathcal{B}} = \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}_{\mathcal{B}}} \cup \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}_{\mathcal{B}}}$ . Finally,  $\mathcal{B}$  hardcodes  $\{\mathsf{sk}_i\}_{i \in \mathcal{N}_{\mathsf{sk}}}$  into D' to produce D and outputs  $(D, \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}_{\mathcal{B}}}, \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}_{\mathcal{B}}})$  to its challenger. Note that by construction it must hold that  $|\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}_{\mathcal{B}}}| \leq \sigma$  and  $|\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}_{\mathcal{B}}}| \leq \rho$ . Denote with  $\mathcal{T}_{\mathcal{B}}'$  the set of traitors as computed by  $\mathcal{B}$ 's challenger when running  $\mathcal{T}_{\mathcal{B}}' \triangleq \Pi$ . Trace D( $\mathsf{pk}$ ,  $\mathsf{tk}$ ,  $\varepsilon$ ,  $\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}_{\mathcal{B}}}$ ,  $\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}_{\mathcal{B}}}$ ,  $\{\mathsf{sk}_i\}_{i \in \mathcal{I}_{\mathcal{B}}}$ ). Then, it holds that  $\mathcal{T}_{\mathcal{A}}' = \mathcal{T}_{\mathcal{B}}' \setminus \mathcal{N}_{\mathsf{sk}}$ .

**Analysis.** First, it is easy to see that if D' is good for  $\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}\mathcal{A}}$  and  $\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}\mathcal{A}}$ , then D is good for  $\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}\mathcal{B}}$  and  $\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}\mathcal{B}}$  and thus  $\Pr[\mathsf{GoodDec}_{\mathcal{A}}] = \Pr[\mathsf{GoodDec}_{\mathcal{B}}]$ .

We start with BadTr: Observe that if BadTr<sub> $\mathcal{A}$ </sub> happens, then there must exist some party  $i \in \mathcal{T}'_{\mathcal{A}}$  such that  $i \notin \mathcal{T}_{\mathcal{A}}$ . In this case, however, it must hold that  $i \in \mathcal{T}'_{\mathcal{B}}$  and  $i \notin \mathcal{N}_{\mathsf{sk}}$ , because  $\mathcal{T}'_{\mathcal{A}} = \mathcal{T}'_{\mathcal{B}} \setminus \mathcal{N}_{\mathsf{sk}}$ . Since  $\mathcal{T}_{\mathcal{B}} = \mathcal{T}_{\mathcal{A}} \cup \mathcal{N}_{\mathsf{sk}}$  and  $i \notin \mathcal{T}_{\mathcal{A}}$  as well as  $i \notin \mathcal{N}_{\mathsf{sk}}$ , it must hold that  $i \notin \mathcal{T}_{\mathcal{B}}$ . In this case, the event  $\mathsf{BadTr}_{\mathcal{B}}$  happens and thus

$$\Pr[\mathsf{BadTr}_{\mathcal{A}}] = \Pr[\mathsf{BadTr}_{\mathcal{B}}],$$

which is negligible by assumption.

Next, we look at GoodTr: Suppose that GoodTr<sub>B</sub> happens. In this case, it holds that  $\mathcal{T}'_{\mathcal{B}} \subseteq \mathcal{T}_{\mathcal{B}}$ . Also, by construction, for all  $i \in \mathcal{T}'_{\mathcal{A}}$  it holds that  $i \in \mathcal{T}'_{\mathcal{B}} \setminus \mathcal{N}_{\mathsf{sk}}$  and thus  $i \in \mathcal{T}_{\mathcal{B}} \setminus \mathcal{N}_{\mathsf{sk}}$ . Since  $\mathcal{T}_{\mathcal{B}} = \mathcal{T}_{\mathcal{A}} \cup \mathcal{N}_{\mathsf{sk}}$ , we get that  $i \in (\mathcal{T}_{\mathcal{A}} \cup \mathcal{N}_{\mathsf{sk}}) \setminus \mathcal{N}_{\mathsf{sk}} = \mathcal{T}_{\mathcal{A}} \setminus \mathcal{N}_{\mathsf{sk}} \subseteq \mathcal{T}_{\mathcal{A}}$  and thus  $\mathcal{T}'_{\mathcal{A}} \subseteq \mathcal{T}_{\mathcal{A}}$ .

Finally, we will show that  $|\mathcal{T}'_{\mathcal{A}}| \geq \tau - \max(|\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}'\mathcal{A}}| - \sigma, 0)$ . If  $\mathsf{GoodTr}_{\mathcal{B}}$  happens, then it must hold that  $|\mathcal{T}'_{\mathcal{B}}| \geq \tau$ . Since  $\mathcal{T}'_{\mathcal{A}} = \mathcal{T}'_{\mathcal{B}} \setminus \mathcal{N}_{\mathsf{sk}}$ , we get that

$$|\mathcal{T}_{\mathcal{A}}'| \ge |\mathcal{T}_{\mathcal{B}}'| - |\mathcal{N}_{\mathsf{sk}}| = |\mathcal{T}_{\mathcal{B}}'| - \max(|\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}}_{\mathcal{A}}'| - \sigma, 0) \ge \tau - \max(|\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}}_{\mathcal{A}}'| - \sigma, 0).$$

We can conclude that

$$\begin{split} &\Pr\left[\mathcal{T}_{\mathcal{A}}' \subseteq \mathcal{T}_{\mathcal{A}} \ \land \ |\mathcal{T}_{\mathcal{A}}'| \geq \tau - \max\left(|\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}_{\mathcal{A}}}'| - \sigma, 0\right)\right] \\ &\geq \Pr[\mathsf{GoodTr}_{\mathcal{B}}] \\ &\geq \Pr[\mathsf{GoodDec}_{\mathcal{B}}] - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda) \\ &= \Pr[\mathsf{GoodDec}_{\mathcal{A}}] - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda). \end{split}$$

#### <span id="page-21-0"></span>5.2 Full-Insider Implies Partial-Insider Resilience

Additionally, we show that resilience against full insiders implies resilience against partial insiders, i.e., that any scheme that is  $\tau$ -traceable against  $(\sigma, \rho)$  insiders is also  $\tau$ -traceable against  $(\sigma - x, \rho + x)$  for all x with  $0 \le x \le \sigma$ . In our compiler, if the tracer receives a decoder D' that works for  $\rho + x$  partial insiders  $\mathcal{I}_{pd}'$ , he designates a subset  $\mathcal{I}_{pd} \subseteq \mathcal{I}_{pd}'$  of size  $\rho$  to be partial insiders against the base scheme, and the remaining x partial insiders as full insiders instead  $\mathcal{I}_{sk} = \mathcal{I}_{sk}' \cup (\mathcal{I}_{pd}' \setminus \mathcal{I}_{pd})$ . Then, he constructs a decoder D against the base scheme. When receiving partial decryptions on behalf of  $\mathcal{I}_{pd}$ , and secret keys on behalf of  $\mathcal{I}_{pd}' \setminus \mathcal{I}_{pd}$ , D uses the given secret keys to compute partial decryptions on behalf of  $\mathcal{I}_{pd}' \setminus \mathcal{I}_{pd}$ , and runs D' with the secret keys of  $\mathcal{I}_{sk}'$ , and the computed partial decryptions of  $\mathcal{I}_{pd}' \setminus \mathcal{I}_{pd}$  alongside the given partial decryptions of  $\mathcal{I}_{pd}$ .

<span id="page-21-1"></span>Construction 2 (Full Insiders to Partial Insiders). Let  $\Pi$  be a threshold KEM that is  $\tau$ -traceable against  $(\sigma, \rho)$ -insiders. We construct  $\Pi'$  which is identical to  $\Pi$  except for a modification to the Trace algorithm:

{22}------------------------------------------------

 $\Pi'$ . Trace  $^{D'}(\mathsf{pk},\mathsf{tk},\varepsilon,\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}}',\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}}',\{\mathsf{sk}_i\}_{i\in\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}}'\cup\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}}'})$ : Let  $I'_{\mathsf{sk}}=|\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}}'|$  and  $I'_{\mathsf{pd}}=|\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}}'|$ . Abort and output  $\mathcal{T}'=\emptyset$  unless all of the following conditions are met:

- $\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}}{}' \cap \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}}{}' = \emptyset$
- $I'_{\sf sk} \leq \sigma$ , i.e., there are at most a tolerable amount of full insiders.
- $I'_{\sf sk} + I'_{\sf pd} \leq \sigma + \rho$ , i.e., let  $x = \sigma I'_{\sf sk}$  be the difference between how many full insiders we could tolerate and how many we received. Then, we can tolerate at most  $I'_{\sf pd} \leq \rho + x$  partial insiders.

Otherwise, proceed with the following steps to sample appropriate sets of full insiders  $\mathcal{I}_{\sf sk}$  and partial insiders  $\mathcal{I}_{\sf pd}$  as well as construct a decoder D to trace using  $\Pi$ . Trace:

• Sample the set  $\mathcal{I}_{pd}$  for  $\Pi$  as an arbitrary subset of size  $\min(\rho, I'_{pd})$  of the set  $\mathcal{I}_{pd}$ , i.e.,

$$\mathcal{I}_{pd} \subseteq \mathcal{I}_{pd}'$$
 and  $|\mathcal{I}_{pd}| = \min(\rho, I'_{pd})$ .

Also, let the set of partial insiders for  $\Pi'$  that are not partial insiders for  $\Pi$  be  $\mathcal{N}_{pd} \leftarrow \mathcal{I}_{pd}' \setminus \mathcal{I}_{pd}$ . These are essentially the set of full insiders that are converted to partial insiders.

- Set the set of full insiders  $\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}} \leftarrow \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}}' \cup \mathcal{N}_{\mathsf{pd}}$ .
- Construct a decoder D that given a KEM-key k, a ciphertext c, a set of secret keys  $\{\overline{\mathsf{sk}}_i\}_{i\in\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}}}$  from parties in  $\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}}$  and partial decryptions  $\{d_i\}_{i\in\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}}}$  from parties  $\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}}$  does the following:
  - Compute  $\{d_i \leftarrow \mathsf{PDec}(\overline{\mathsf{sk}}_i, c)\}_{i \in \mathcal{N}_{\mathsf{pd}}}$ , i.e., compute partial decryptions on behalf of the full insiders that are converted to partial insiders.
  - Output  $D'(k, c, \{\overline{\mathsf{sk}_i}\}_{i \in \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}'}}, \{d_i\}_{i \in \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}'}}).$

Finally, run and output  $\mathcal{T}' \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \Pi$ . Trace  $^D(\mathsf{pk}, \mathsf{tk}, \varepsilon, \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}}, \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}}, \{\mathsf{sk}_i\}_{i \in \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{cl}} \cup \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{nd}}})$ .

<span id="page-22-0"></span>**Theorem 5.3** Let  $\Pi$  be a TT-KEM that is  $\tau$ -traceable against  $(\sigma, \rho)$ -insiders. Then Construction 2 is  $\tau$  traceable against  $(\sigma - x, \rho + x)$  insiders for all  $0 \le x \le \sigma$ .

*Proof of Theorem 5.3.* Fix arbitrary  $\tau, \sigma$ , and  $\rho$  for a base scheme  $\Pi$  such that  $0 < \tau \le t$  and  $0 < \tau + \sigma + \rho \le t$  and assume that  $\Pi$  is  $\tau$ -traceable against  $(\sigma, \rho)$  insiders. Let  $\mathcal{A}$  be any PPT adversary against traceability of  $\Pi'$ .

In the following, we introduce a number of random variables for  $\mathcal{A}$  running in Game-Tr. Denote with  $\mathcal{T}_{\mathcal{A}}$  the random variable capturing the set of traitors corrupted by  $\mathcal{A}$  through its corruption oracle in Game-Tr, and with  $\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}'_{\mathcal{A}}}$  as well as  $\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}'_{\mathcal{A}}}$  the set of secret key and partial decryption insiders output by  $\mathcal{A}$ . Denote  $\mathcal{I}'_{\mathcal{A}} = \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}'_{\mathcal{A}}} \cup \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}'_{\mathcal{A}}}$ . W.l.o.g., assume that  $\mathcal{I}'_{\mathcal{A}} \subseteq [n]$ ,  $\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}'_{\mathcal{A}}} \cap \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}'_{\mathcal{A}}} = \emptyset$ ,  $|\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}'_{\mathcal{A}}}| \leq \sigma$ , and  $|\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}'_{\mathcal{A}}}| \leq \rho + \sigma - |\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}'_{\mathcal{A}}}|$ . Also, denote with D' the decoder produced by  $\mathcal{A}$  and by  $\mathcal{T}'_{\mathcal{A}}$  the set of traitors found when tracing D' against  $\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}'_{\mathcal{A}}}$  and  $\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}'_{\mathcal{A}}}$ . We aim to show that there exists a negligible function negl such that

$$\Pr[\mathcal{T}_{\mathcal{A}}' \subseteq \mathcal{T}_{\mathcal{A}} \ \land \ |\mathcal{T}_{\mathcal{A}}'| \geq \tau] \geq \Pr[\mathsf{GoodDec}_{\mathcal{A}}] - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$$

as well as

$$\Pr[\mathsf{BadTr}_{\mathcal{A}}] \leq \mathsf{negl}(\lambda).$$

We construct a reductio  $\mathcal{B}$  that tries to break  $\tau$ -traceability against  $(\sigma, \rho)$ -insiders of  $\Pi$  as follows: When  $\mathcal{B}$  receives public parameters and the public key from its challenger,  $\mathcal{B}$  forwards those to  $\mathcal{A}$ . When  $\mathcal{A}$  issues a corruption query,  $\mathcal{B}$  forwards it to its challenger and returns the resulting secret key to  $\mathcal{A}$ . Similarly,  $\mathcal{B}$  answers queries to  $\mathcal{O}^{\mathsf{PDec-Hon}}$  by querying its own challenger's partial decryption oracle. As a result, when  $\mathcal{A}$  outputs  $(D', \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}'}, \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}'})$ , it holds that  $\mathcal{T}_{\mathcal{A}} = \mathcal{T}_{\mathcal{B}}$ .

Given the decoder D',  $\mathcal{B}$  must produce a decoder D to return to its challenger. To do so,  $\mathcal{B}$  follows the procedure outlined in  $\Pi'$ . Trace. In particular,  $\mathcal{B}$  samples the sets  $\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}_{\mathcal{B}}}$  as an arbitrary subset of size  $\min(\rho, |\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}_{\mathcal{A}}}|)$  of  $\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}_{\mathcal{A}}}$ . It computes  $\mathcal{N}_{\mathsf{pd}} \leftarrow \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}_{\mathcal{A}}} \setminus \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}_{\mathcal{B}}}$  and sets  $\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}_{\mathcal{B}}} \leftarrow \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}_{\mathcal{A}}} \cup \mathcal{N}_{\mathsf{pd}}$ . It constructs a decoder D that, on input  $(k, c, \{\overline{\mathsf{sk}_i}\}_{i \in \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}_{\mathcal{B}}}}, \{d_i\}_{i \in \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}_{\mathcal{B}}}})$ , computes  $d_i \leftarrow \mathsf{PDec}(\overline{\mathsf{sk}_i}, c)$  for all  $i \in \mathcal{N}_{\mathsf{pd}}$  and returns the result of the query

$$D'\left(k, c, \{\overline{\mathsf{sk}_i}\}_{i \in \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}'_{\mathcal{A}}}}, \{d_i\}_{i \in \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}'_{\mathcal{A}}}}\right).$$

{23}------------------------------------------------

Note that the above is possible, because  $\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}'_{\mathcal{A}}} \subseteq \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}\mathcal{B}}$ ,  $\mathcal{N}_{\mathsf{pd}} \subseteq \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}\mathcal{B}}$ , i.e., D gets  $\overline{\mathsf{sk}_i}$  as input for all  $i \in \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}'_{\mathcal{A}}}$  and  $i \in \mathcal{N}_{\mathsf{pd}}$ . Also, observe that  $\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}'_{\mathcal{A}}} = \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}_{\mathcal{B}}} \cup \mathcal{N}_{\mathsf{pd}}$ , hence the decoder D can compute all necessary partial decryptions from its input. Finally, the reduction  $\mathcal{B}$  outputs  $(D, \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}\mathcal{B}}, \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}\mathcal{B}})$  to its challenger. Denote with  $\mathcal{T}'_{\mathcal{B}}$  the set of traitors identified when D is traced by  $\mathcal{B}$ 's challenger. Observe that  $\mathcal{B}$ 's simulation is perfect, and thus  $\mathcal{T}'_{\mathcal{B}} = \mathcal{T}'_{\mathcal{A}}$ .

**Analysis.** First, observe that if D' is good for  $\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}'\mathcal{A}}$  and  $\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}'\mathcal{A}}$ , then D is also good for  $\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}\mathcal{B}}$  and  $\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}\mathcal{B}}$ . Similarly, if D' is not good for  $\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}'\mathcal{A}}$  and  $\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}'\mathcal{A}}$ , then D is also not good for  $\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{sk}\mathcal{B}}$  and  $\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}\mathcal{B}}$ . Hence, it holds that  $\mathsf{GoodDec}_{\mathcal{A}} = \mathsf{GoodDec}_{\mathcal{B}}$  and thus  $\mathsf{Pr}[\mathsf{GoodDec}_{\mathcal{A}}] = \mathsf{Pr}[\mathsf{GoodDec}_{\mathcal{B}}]$ .

We start with BadTr: Clearly, if BadTr<sub>A</sub> happens, then it must hold that  $\mathcal{T}'_{\mathcal{A}} \not\subseteq \mathcal{T}_{\mathcal{A}}$ . Since  $\mathcal{T}'_{\mathcal{A}} = \mathcal{T}'_{\mathcal{B}}$  and  $\mathcal{T}_{\mathcal{A}} = \mathcal{T}_{\mathcal{B}}$ , it must also holds that  $\mathcal{T}'_{\mathcal{B}} \not\subseteq \mathcal{T}_{\mathcal{B}}$  and thus BadTr<sub>B</sub> happens. We get that  $\Pr[\mathsf{BadTr}_{\mathcal{A}}] = \Pr[\mathsf{BadTr}_{\mathcal{B}}]$ , which is negligible by assumption.

Next, we look at  $\mathsf{GoodTr}$ : Suppose that  $\mathsf{GoodTr}_{\mathcal{B}}$  happens. In this case, it holds that  $\mathcal{T}'_{\mathcal{B}} \subseteq \mathcal{T}_{\mathcal{B}}$  and  $|\mathcal{T}'_{\mathcal{B}}| \geq \tau$ . Again, since  $\mathcal{T}'_{\mathcal{A}} = \mathcal{T}'_{\mathcal{B}}$  and  $\mathcal{T}_{\mathcal{A}} = \mathcal{T}_{\mathcal{B}}$ , it follows that  $\mathcal{T}'_{\mathcal{A}} \subseteq \mathcal{T}_{\mathcal{A}}$  and  $|\mathcal{T}'_{\mathcal{A}}| \geq \tau$  whenever  $\mathsf{GoodTr}_{\mathcal{B}}$  happens. We conclude that

$$\Pr[\mathsf{GoodTr}_{\mathcal{A}}] \geq \Pr[\mathsf{GoodTr}_{\mathcal{B}}] \geq \Pr[\mathsf{GoodDec}_{\mathcal{B}}] - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda) = \Pr[\mathsf{GoodDec}_{\mathcal{A}}] - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda),$$

for a negligible function  $\operatorname{\mathsf{negl}}(\lambda)$  by assumption of  $\tau$ -traceability of  $\Pi$  against  $(\sigma, \rho)$  insiders.

# <span id="page-23-0"></span>6 Achieving K-traceability for Constant K

In this section, we present a compiler that allows us to identify a constant number of traitors K by partitioning parties into K bins.

<span id="page-23-1"></span>Construction 3 (1-Partition Compiler). Let  $\Pi$  be a perfect  $\tau$ -traceable threshold KEM against  $\rho$  partial insiders for key space  $\mathcal{K} = \{0,1\}^{\lambda}$ . Let  $0 < \delta < 1$ . Then  $\Pi'$  with reconstruction threshold  $\mathcal{S}_n = \{n/2\}$  and security threshold  $t(r) = (1 - \delta)r = (1 - \delta)n/2$  is constructed as follows.

 $\Pi'$ .KGen $(1^{\lambda}, n, r, t, \varepsilon)$ : Sample a (K, n)-balanced partition  $P = \{B_1, \dots, B_K\}$  of parties in [n] uniformly at random. Then, run the key generation algorithm of  $\Pi$  in each bin with threshold  $t_{\sf bin} = (1 - \delta)n/2K$ :

$$\left\{ \left(\mathsf{pk}_{j}, \left\{\mathsf{sk}_{i}\right\}_{i \in [B_{j}]}, \mathsf{tk}_{j}\right) \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \Pi.\mathsf{KGen}\left(1^{\lambda}, B_{j}, t_{\mathsf{bin}}, \varepsilon/4\right) \right\}_{j \in [K]}$$

Output  $\mathsf{pk} \coloneqq \{\mathsf{pk}_j\}_{j \in [K]}, \, \{\mathsf{sk}_i\}_{i \in [n]}, \, \text{and } \mathsf{tk} \coloneqq \{\mathsf{tk}_j\}_{j \in [K]}.$ 

 $\Pi'$ .Enc(pk): Run encryption  $(k_j, c_j) \stackrel{\hspace{0.1em}\mathsf{\scriptscriptstyle\$}}{\leftarrow} \Pi$ .Enc(pk<sub>j</sub>) in each bin  $j \in [K]$ . Compute  $k \leftarrow \bigoplus_{j \in [K]} k_j$  and  $c \leftarrow (c_1, \ldots, c_K)$ . Output (k, c).

 $\Pi'$ .PDec( $\mathsf{sk}_i, (c_1, \ldots, c_K)$ ): Let  $j = \mathsf{bin}(P, i)$  and output  $d_i \leftarrow \Pi$ .PDec( $\mathsf{sk}_i, c_j$ ).

 $\Pi'$ .Combine(pk, S,  $\{d_i\}_{i\in[n]}, (c_1, \ldots, c_K)$ ): Given partial decryptions from a set of parties S, verify that  $|S\cap B_j| \geq t_{\text{bin}}$  for all  $j\in[K]$ . Then, recover  $k_j \leftarrow \Pi$ .Combine $(S\cap B_j, \{d_i\}_{S\cap B_j}, c_j)$  for all  $j\in[K]$ . Output  $k\leftarrow \bigoplus_{j\in[K]} k_j$ .

 $\Pi'$ . Trace  $^{D(\cdot)}(\mathsf{pk},\mathsf{tk},\varepsilon,\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}},\{\mathsf{sk}_i\}_{i\in\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}}})$ : Let  $\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}}^{(j)}=\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}}\cap B_j$  for all  $j\in[K]$ . Given black-box access to a decoder D we first test it by running test  $\leftarrow$  TestDec $(\mathsf{pk},\emptyset,\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}},\{\mathsf{sk}_i\}_{i\in\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}}},Q\coloneqq 8\lambda/\varepsilon^2,\varepsilon/2)$ . (See Figure 4). If test = 1, we say that D tests good. If test = 0, we set all  $D_j$  to the Dummy decoder that always returns 0.

Otherwise, for all  $j \in [K]$  where  $\mathcal{I}_{pd}^{(j)} \leq \rho$ , construct the decoder  $D_j$  as follows: On input the tuple  $(k_j, c_j, \{d_i\}_{i \in \mathcal{I}_{pd}^{(j)}})$ , compute for all  $\ell \in [K] \setminus \{j\}$ :

$$(k_{\ell}, c_{\ell}) \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \Pi.\mathsf{Enc}(\mathsf{pk}_{\ell}) \text{ and } \forall i \in \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}}^{(\ell)} \colon d_i \leftarrow \Pi.\mathsf{PDec}(\mathsf{sk}_i, c_{\ell}).$$

Compute  $k \leftarrow \bigoplus_{u \in [K]} k_u$  and return  $D(k, (c_1, \dots, c_j, \dots, c_K), \{d_i\}_{i \in \mathcal{I}_{pd}})$  as  $D_j$ 's output.

Finally, for all  $j \in [K]$ , where  $\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}}^{(j)} \leq \rho$ , run  $\mathcal{T}_j \stackrel{\hspace{0.1em}\mathsf{\scriptscriptstyle\$}}{\leftarrow} \Pi.\mathsf{Trace}^{D_j(\cdot)}(\mathsf{pk}_j,\mathsf{tk}_j,\varepsilon/4)$ . For all  $j \in [K]$  where  $\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}}^{(j)} > \rho$ , set  $\mathcal{T}_j \leftarrow \emptyset$ . Output  $\mathcal{T} \leftarrow \bigcup_{j \in [K]} \mathcal{T}_j$ .

{24}------------------------------------------------

**Parameter Sizes.** If  $\Pi$  has ciphertext size C(n), public key size P(n), and secret key size S(n), then  $\Pi'$  has sizes  $P'(n) = K \cdot P(n/K)$ , S'(n) = S(n/K), and  $C'(n) = K \cdot C(n/K)$ .  $\Pi'$  has keyspace  $\mathcal{K}_{\lambda} = \{0, 1\}^{\lambda}$ .

Remark 6.1 In Construction 3, we instantiate the underlying scheme in each bin with limit  $\varepsilon/4$  to allow for a small margin of error when testing decoders. Essentially, in traceability proof, we need to claim that if D is  $\varepsilon$ -good against  $\Pi'$ , then, by Chernoff's bound, D must test to be at least  $(\varepsilon/2)$ -good except with negligible probability, and if any decoder D tests at least  $(\varepsilon/2)$ -good, then the decoders  $D_j$  must be at least  $(\varepsilon/4)$ -good, which, again, holds by Chernoff's bound. Note that, if the underlying scheme is unable to satisfy this requirement due to a restriction on its limit, one can run the limit-elimination compiler (Theorem B.2) first.

## <span id="page-24-0"></span>6.1 Correctness, Robustness, and Semantic Security of Construction 3

To prove probabilistic correctness and robustness of Construction 3, we introduce the following Lemma, a proof of which can be found in Appendix A.2.

<span id="page-24-1"></span>**Lemma 6.2** Let  $n = \operatorname{poly}(\lambda)$  and K = o(n). Further, let  $P_j = \{B_i^{(j)}\}_{i \in [K]}$  for  $j \in [\ell]$  be a collection of  $\ell$  independently and uniformly sampled (K,n)-balanced partitions, where  $|B_i^{(j)}| = n/K$  for every  $i \in [K]$  and every  $j \in [\ell]$ . Let  $t_{\mathsf{bin}} = \frac{n}{2K} - \sqrt{\frac{\lambda n}{K}}$ . Then,

1. For any  $\ell \geq 1$ , for uniformly distributed  $S \subseteq [n]$  where  $|S| \geq n/2$ , there exists some  $j \in [\ell]$  such that for all  $i \in [K]$ ,

$$|S \cap B_i^{(j)}| \geq t_{\mathsf{bin}},$$

except with negligible probability in  $\lambda$ .

2. Let  $r = n/K - t_{\text{bin}}$ ,  $\mathbf{r} = r \cdot (1, \dots, 1) \in \mathbb{N}^K$ , and  $c \in (0, 1/2)$ . Then, for  $\ell \geq 2(1 - c)K/c^2$ , the probability that there is a subset  $S \subseteq [n]$ , where  $|S| \leq n/2 - cn$ , which  $(\ell, \mathbf{r})$ -blocks  $\{P_j\}_{j \in [\ell]}$  is negligible in  $\lambda$ .

**Lemma 6.3** For  $\delta \geq 2\sqrt{\lambda K/n}$ , Construction 3 is probabilistically correct,  $\frac{n(1+\delta)}{2K}$ -robust, and semantically secure.

Proof of Probabilistic Correctness of Construction 3. Consider a random set  $|S| \le n/2$ . We prove in Part 1 of Lemma 6.2 that S has at least  $t_{\text{bin}}$  parties from every one of the K bins. Thus, correctness follows.

Proof of Robustness of Construction 3. Clearly, an adversary can only break robustness by causing sufficient crashes in at least one bin to break decryption. Since  $\Pi$  is assumed to be perfectly robust, any adversary must crash more than

$$\frac{n}{K} - t_{\mathsf{bin}} = \frac{n}{2K} \cdot (1 + \delta)$$

parties in any of the bins.

Proof of Semantic Security of Construction 3. Fix arbitrary  $\lambda, n \in \mathbb{N}$ , and  $\varepsilon \in (0, 1/2]$ . Let r = n/2,  $t = (n/2) \cdot (1 - \delta)$ , and  $t_{\text{bin}} = t/K$ . Let  $\mathcal{A}$  be any PPT adversary against Game-IND-CPA<sup>II</sup> $(1^{\lambda}, n, r, t, \varepsilon)$ . We construct a PPT reduction  $\mathcal{B}$  against Game-IND-CPA<sup>II</sup> $(1^{\lambda}, n/K, t_{\text{bin}}, t_{\text{bin}}, \varepsilon/4)$  as follows: First,  $\mathcal{B}$  runs  $\mathcal{A}(1^{\lambda}, n, r, t, \varepsilon)$  to obtain a set of corrupted parties Cor. Assume w.l.o.g. that  $\text{Cor} \subseteq [n]$  and |Cor| < t. Then,  $\mathcal{B}$  simulates key generation by first sampling a random (K, n)-balanced partition  $P = \{B_j\}_{j \in [K]}$ .  $\mathcal{B}$  then chooses any  $j^* \in [K]$  such that  $|B_{j^*} \cap \text{Cor}| < t_{\text{bin}}$ . Note that such  $j^*$  must always exist if |Cor| < t, because  $t_{\text{bin}} \cdot K = t > |\text{Cor}|$ . Then,  $\mathcal{B}$  forwards  $\text{Cor}_{j^*} = \text{Cor} \cap B_{j^*}$  to its challenger, and receives  $\mathsf{pk}_{j^*}$ ,  $\{\mathsf{sk}_i\}_{i \in \mathsf{Cor}_{j^*}}$ ,  $\mathsf{tk}_j^*$ , as well as the challenge  $(k_j^*, c_j^*)$ . Then,  $\mathcal{B}$  simulates key generation in all remaining bins according to protocol, generating

$$\left(\mathsf{pk}_j, \{\mathsf{sk}_i\}_{i \in B_j}, \mathsf{tk}_j\right) \overset{\hspace{0.1em}\mathsf{\scriptscriptstyle\$}}{\leftarrow} \Pi.\mathsf{KGen}(1^\lambda, B_j, t_{\mathsf{bin}}, t_{\mathsf{bin}}, \varepsilon/4) \ \text{ for all } j \neq j^*.$$

<span id="page-24-2"></span><sup>&</sup>lt;sup>7</sup>To avoid unnecessary notation overhead of relabeling parties, assume that the challenger runs key generation for participant indices  $\mathcal{I}_{pd}$ .

{25}------------------------------------------------

To simulate the challenge ciphertext,  $\mathcal{B}$  samples  $(k_j, c_j) \stackrel{\hspace{0.1em}\mathsf{\scriptscriptstyle\$}}{\leftarrow} \Pi.\mathsf{Enc}(\mathsf{pk}_j)$  for all  $j \neq j$ , and sets  $k^* \leftarrow \bigoplus_{j \in [K]} k_j$  as well as  $c^* \leftarrow \{c_j\}_{j \in [K]}$ .  $\mathcal{B}$  runs

$$\mathcal{A}\Big(\{\mathsf{pk}_j\}_{j\in[K]},\{\mathsf{tk}_j\}_{j\in[K]},\{\mathsf{sk}_i\}_{i\in\mathsf{Cor}},k^*,c^*\Big)\,,$$

obtaining the bit b', and outputs the same bit b' to its challenger.

Analysis. Let b be the internal bit of  $\mathcal{B}$ 's challenger in Game-IND-CPA $_{\mathcal{B}}^{\Pi}$  and let  $\beta$  be the hypothetical internal bit of  $\mathcal{B}$ 's simulation of Game-IND-CPA $_{\mathcal{A}}^{\Pi'}$ . If b=0, then  $k_{j^*}$  is a real key, and thus  $\mathcal{B}$  simulates Game-IND-CPA $_{\mathcal{A}}^{\Pi'}$  perfectly for  $\beta=0$ . If b=1, then  $k_{j^*}$  is a uniform random value from  $\mathcal{K}_{\lambda}$ , and thus  $k^*$  is also uniformly random by the perfect security of the one-time pad, and thus  $\mathcal{B}$  perfectly simulates Game-IND-CPA $_{\mathcal{A}}^{\Pi'}$  for  $\beta=1$ . We get that

$$\Pr[\mathsf{Game\text{-}IND\text{-}CPA}_{\mathcal{A}}^{\Pi'}=1] = \Pr[\mathsf{Game\text{-}IND\text{-}CPA}_{\mathcal{B}}^{\Pi'}=1],$$

which is  $\leq 1/2 + \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$  by assumption for a negligible function  $\mathsf{negl}$ .

## <span id="page-25-0"></span>6.2 Traceability of the 1-Partition Compiler

<span id="page-25-1"></span>**Theorem 6.4** Let  $K \in \mathbb{N}$  be the number of bins used in Construction 3. Let  $\tau > 0$  and  $\tau + \rho \leq t_{\text{bin}}$ . If the underlying TT-KEM  $\Pi$  is  $\tau$ -traceable against  $\rho$  partial insiders then  $\Pi'$  (Construction 3) is  $(\tau' = (K-x) \cdot \tau)$ -traceable against  $(\rho' = \rho + x \cdot (\rho + 1))$  partial insiders for all  $0 \leq x < K$ . Whenever  $\rho' > 0$ , we require that  $\Pi$  offers a partial decryption oracle  $\mathcal{O}^{\mathsf{PDec-Hon}}$ . If  $\Pi$  offers a partial decryption oracle  $\mathcal{O}^{\mathsf{PDec-Hon}}$ , then so does  $\Pi'$ .

To prove Theorem 6.4, we first prove the following intuitive lemma, which argues that the decoders  $D_j$  constructed by the tracer in Construction 3 are equally good as the underlying decoder D.

<span id="page-25-2"></span>**Lemma 6.5** For all j it holds that  $P_{\Pi'}(D) = P_{\Pi}(D_j)$ , where D is the decoder that is traced in  $\Pi'$  and  $D_j$  is the decoder for the j-th instance of  $\Pi$  that is constructed by  $\Pi'$ . Trace (before it is potentially replaced with the dummy decoder).

Proof of Lemma 6.5. Fix an arbitrary  $j \in [K]$  and let  $(pk := \{pk_\ell\}_{\ell \in [K]}, sk, tk) \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \Pi'.\mathsf{KGen}(*)$ . Fix  $\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}} \subseteq [n]$ . Let D be an arbitrary decoder and  $D_j$  be the decoder that is constructed by  $\Pi'.\mathsf{Trace}$  for instance j before it is potentially replaced with the dummy decoder. When instantiating the definition of P with  $\Pi'$ , we get that

$$\begin{split} &P_{\Pi'}(D) \\ &= \Pr \left[ D\Big(k^b, (c_1, \dots, c_K), \left\{d_i\right\}_{i \in \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}}}\Big) = b \colon \begin{array}{c} \{(c_\ell, k_\ell) \xleftarrow{\$} \Pi.\mathsf{Enc}(\mathsf{pk}_\ell)\}_{\ell \in [K]} \\ \{d_i \leftarrow \Pi.\mathsf{PDec}(\mathsf{sk}_i, c_\ell)\}_{\ell \in [K], i \in \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}} \cap B_\ell} \\ k^0 \xleftarrow{\$} \bigoplus_{\ell=1}^K k_\ell \\ k_1 \xleftarrow{\$} \mathcal{K}, b \xleftarrow{\$} \{0, 1\} \end{array} \right] \\ &= \Pr \left[ D\Big(k, (c_1, \dots, c_K), \left\{d_i\right\}_{i \in \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}}}\Big) = b \colon \begin{array}{c} \{(c_\ell, k_\ell) \xleftarrow{\$} \Pi.\mathsf{Enc}(\mathsf{pk}_\ell)\}_{\ell \in [K], i \in \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}} \cap B_\ell} \\ \{d_i \leftarrow \Pi.\mathsf{PDec}(\mathsf{sk}_i, c_\ell)\}_{\ell \in [K], i \in \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}} \cap B_\ell} \\ k_j^0 \leftarrow k_j, k_j^1 \xleftarrow{\$} \mathcal{K}, b \xleftarrow{\$} \{0, 1\} \\ k \leftarrow k_j^0 \oplus \bigoplus_{\ell \in [K] \backslash \{j\}} k_\ell \end{array} \right]. \end{split}$$

The above equality holds. To see this, observe that for b = 0, both experiments are identical. When b = 1, we have  $k_i^b = k_1^1 \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathcal{K}$ , and thus the two ditribuisions are identical:

$$\left(k \leftarrow k_j^b \oplus \bigoplus_{\ell \in [K] \setminus \{j\}} k_\ell\right) \equiv (k \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathcal{K}).$$

{26}------------------------------------------------

Next, let us instantiate  $P_{\Pi}(D_i)$ . We get that

$$P_{\Pi}(D_{j})$$

$$= \Pr \left[ D_{j} \left( k_{j}^{b}, c_{j}, \{d_{i}\}_{i \in \mathcal{I}_{pd} \cap B_{j}} \right) = b \colon \begin{cases} (c_{j}, k_{j}^{0}) \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \Pi.\mathsf{Enc}(\mathsf{pk}_{j}) \\ d_{i} \leftarrow \Pi.\mathsf{PDec}(\mathsf{sk}_{i}, c_{j}) \}_{i \in \mathcal{I}_{pd} \cap B_{j}} \\ k_{j}^{1} \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathcal{K}, b \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \{0, 1\} \end{cases} \right]$$

$$= \Pr \left[ D\left( k, \{c_{\ell}\}_{\ell \in [K]}, \{d_{i}\}_{i \in \mathcal{I}_{pd}} \right) = b \colon \begin{cases} (c_{\ell}, k_{\ell}) \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \Pi.\mathsf{Enc}(\mathsf{pk}_{\ell}) \}_{\ell \in [K] \setminus \{j\}} \\ (c_{j}, k_{j}^{0}) \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \Pi.\mathsf{Enc}(\mathsf{pk}_{j}) \end{cases} \right]$$

$$= \Pr \left[ D\left( k, \{c_{\ell}\}_{\ell \in [K]}, \{d_{i}\}_{i \in \mathcal{I}_{pd}} \right) = b \colon \begin{cases} d_{i} \leftarrow \Pi.\mathsf{PDec}(\mathsf{sk}_{i}, c_{\ell}) \}_{\ell \in [K], i \in \mathcal{I}_{pd} \cap B_{\ell}} \\ k_{j}^{1} \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathcal{K}, b \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \{0, 1\} \\ k \leftarrow k_{j}^{b} \oplus \bigoplus_{\ell \in [K] \setminus \{j\}} k_{\ell} \end{cases} \right]$$

$$= P_{\Pi'}(D),$$

where in the second step, we inlined the construction of  $D_j$  with respect to D as defined by  $\Pi$ . Trace.

Equipped with Lemma 6.5, we can now prove Theorem 6.4.

Proof of Theorem 6.4. Fix an arbitrary x with  $0 \le x < K$  and assume that  $\Pi$  is  $\tau$ -traceable against  $\rho$  partial insiders, where  $\tau > 0$  and  $\tau + \rho \le t_{\mathsf{bin}}$ . Let  $\tau' = (K - x) \cdot \tau$  and  $\rho' = \rho + x \cdot (\rho + 1)$ . We aim to prove  $\tau'$ -traceability against  $\rho'$  partial insiders of  $\Pi'$ .

Denote with  $\mathcal{T}'$  the set of traitors identified as in Game-Tr (Figure 3). Denote for all  $j \in [K]$  with  $\mathcal{T}'_j = B_j \cap \mathcal{T}'$  the set of traitors identified from  $B_j$  and with  $\mathcal{T}_j = \mathcal{T} \cap B_j$  the set of real traitors from  $B_j$ . In the following proof, assume w.l.o.g. that for all adversaries against Game-Tr of  $\Pi'$ , it holds that  $|\mathcal{I}_{pd}| < \rho'$ .

Intuitively, our proof works as follows: We will show that in all bins  $B_j$  where the adversary asked for at most  $\rho$  partial insiders, tracing will succeed, and we will find at least  $\tau$  traitors due to  $\tau$ -traceability against  $\rho$  partial insiders of  $\Pi$ . Then, a counting argument shows that if  $|\mathcal{I}_{pd}| \leq \rho'$ , there can be at most x bins  $B_j$ , where  $|\mathcal{I}_{pd}|^{(j)}| > \rho$ , and thus we find  $\tau$  traitors in all remaining K - x bins. We next formalize this intuition.

First, we define the following two events for all  $j \in [K]$ :

- GoodTrBin<sub>j</sub>: This event occurs whenever both  $|\mathcal{T}'_j| \geq \tau$  and  $\mathcal{T}'_j \subseteq \mathcal{T}_j$ .
- $\mathsf{BadTrBin}_j$ : This event occurs whenever  $\mathcal{T}'_j \not\subseteq \mathcal{T}_j$ .

Let  $\mathcal{H}_0$  be the  $\tau'$ -traceability game (Definition 4.1) against  $\rho'$  partial insiders, instantiated with  $\Pi'$ . For  $u \in [K]$ , let  $\mathcal{H}_u$  be the same game instantiated except with a modified winning condition. In  $\mathcal{H}_u$ , the additional condition triggers if the adversary manages to avoid being traced or to frame an honest party in  $B_j$  for some  $j \leq u$ . More formally, in  $\mathcal{H}_u$ , we set  $\mathsf{BadTr}$  to 0, whenever  $\mathsf{BadTrBin}_j = 1$  for some  $j \leq u$ , and we set  $\mathsf{GoodTr}$  to test, whenever there exists some  $j \leq u$  for which  $\mathsf{GoodTrBin}_j = 0$  and  $|\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}}^{(j)}| \leq \rho$ , where test is the event that the decoder D passes the test described in the tracing procedure.

Now, observe that  $\Pi'$  is naively  $\tau'$ -traceable against  $\rho'$  partial insiders with respect to  $\mathcal{H}_K$ . To show this, we prove that for all PPT adversaries  $\mathcal{A}$  it holds that  $\Pr[\mathsf{GoodTr}_{\mathcal{A}}^{(K)}] \geq \Pr[\mathsf{GoodDec}_{\mathcal{A}}^{(K)}] - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$ , and  $\Pr[\mathsf{BadTr}_{\mathcal{A}}^{(K)}] = 0$ . In particular, let  $\mathcal{A}$  be any PPT adversary. If  $\mathcal{A}$  hits any event  $\mathsf{BadTrBin}_j$  for  $j \in [K]$ , then  $\mathsf{BadTr}_{\mathcal{A}}^{(K)}$  is set to 0 by definition. If, however,  $\mathcal{A}$  avoids triggering this condition, it must cause  $\mathcal{T}_j' \subseteq \mathcal{T}_j$  for all  $j \in [K]$ . As a consequence, the event  $\mathsf{BadTr}$  cannot occur, because

$$\mathcal{T}' = \bigcup_{j=1}^K \mathcal{T}'_j \subseteq \bigcup_{j=1}^K \mathcal{T}_j = \mathcal{T}.$$

A similar argument holds for  $\mathsf{GoodTr}_{\mathcal{A}}^{(K)}$ . Suppose  $\mathcal{A}$  avoids hitting the condition, i.e. for all  $j \in [K]$  with  $|\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}}^{(j)}| \leq \rho$  it holds that  $\mathsf{GoodTrBin}_j = 1$ . Then,  $\mathcal{T}_j' \subseteq \mathcal{T}_j$  for all  $j \in [K]^8$ , and because  $|\mathcal{T}_j'| \geq \tau$  for

<span id="page-26-0"></span><sup>&</sup>lt;sup>8</sup>Note that in those bins where  $\mathcal{I}_{pd}^{(j)} > \rho$ , the construction sets  $\mathcal{T}'_j$  to  $\emptyset$  and thus  $\mathcal{T}'_j \subseteq \mathcal{T}_j$  holds trivially for such bins.

{27}------------------------------------------------

all  $j \in [K]$  where  $|\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}}^{(j)}| \leq \rho$ , it holds that

$$|\mathcal{T}'| = \sum_{j=1}^{K} |\mathcal{T}'_j| \ge \sum_{j \in [K] \text{ s.t. } |\mathcal{I}_{pd}^{(j)}| \le \rho} \tau \ge (K - x) \cdot \tau = \tau',$$

which causes  $\mathsf{GoodTr}^{(K)}$  to be set to 1. If, however,  $\mathcal{A}$  does trigger the additional condition, then  $\mathsf{GoodTr}^{(K)}$  is set to test. It remains to show that we can bound the probability that test does not happen when  $\mathcal{A}$  produces a good decoder with a negligible function.

<span id="page-27-0"></span>Claim 6.6 If D is  $\varepsilon$ -good, then test = 0 can happen with at most negligible probability.

*Proof of Claim 6.6.* Suppose D is  $\varepsilon$ -good. Let the random variable X count the number of successful tests on D and let N denote the number of trials. Further, we can bound the mean  $\mu = N \cdot P(D) \ge N \cdot (1/2 + \varepsilon)$  We are interested in

$$\Pr[\mathsf{test} = 0 | D \text{ is } \varepsilon\text{-good}] = \Pr[X < N \cdot (1/2 + \varepsilon/2)],$$

and applying the Hoeffding inequality with  $t = N\varepsilon/2$ , we get that

$$\Pr[\mathsf{test} = 0 | D \text{ is } \varepsilon\text{-good}] \leq \Pr[X \leq \mu - t] \leq \exp\left(-\frac{N\varepsilon^2}{2}\right),$$

which is negligible for  $N \ge 2\lambda/\varepsilon^2$ . Since we set  $Q = 8\lambda/\varepsilon^2 \ge 2\lambda/\varepsilon^2$  in the construction, the probability is negligible.

As a result, we get that,  $\Pr\left[\mathsf{GoodTr}_{\mathcal{A}}^{(K)}\right] \ge \Pr\left[\mathsf{GoodDec}_{\mathcal{A}}\right] - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$ .

Hence, in order to show  $\tau'$ -traceability, it remains to show that for all PPT adversaries  $\mathcal{A}$ , it holds that

$$\Pr \Big[ \mathsf{GoodTr}_{\mathcal{A}}^{(0)} ] \geq \Pr [\mathsf{GoodTr}_{\mathcal{A}}^{(K)} \Big] - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda) \ \ \mathrm{and} \ \ \Pr \Big[ \mathsf{BadTr}_{\mathcal{A}}^{(0)} \Big] \leq \Pr \Big[ \mathsf{BadTr}_{\mathcal{A}}^{(K)} \Big] + \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$$

for a negligible function negl.

Let  $\mathcal{A}$  be any PPT adversary. We use  $\mathcal{A}$  to construct a PPT adversary  $\mathcal{B}$  against  $\tau$ -traceability of  $\Pi$  against  $\rho$  partial insiders as follows: First,  $\mathcal{B}$  picks an index  $u \overset{\$}{=} [K]$  uniformly at random. For all indices  $j \neq u$ ,  $\mathcal{B}$  runs the key generation algorithm of  $\Pi$  to generate  $\mathsf{pk}_j$ ,  $\{\mathsf{sk}_i\}_{i \in B_j}$ , and  $\mathsf{tk}_j$  according to protocol.  $\mathcal{B}$  embeds the challenge public key  $\mathsf{pk}^*$ , as received by  $\mathsf{Game-Tr}$  of  $\Pi$ , for instance u, i.e.,  $\mathsf{pk}_u \leftarrow \mathsf{pk}^*$ . Then,  $\mathcal{B}$  runs  $\mathcal{A}$ , simulating corruption queries for parties in  $B_u$  by making use of its own corruption oracle for  $\Pi$ . If applicable,  $\mathcal{B}$  simulates  $\mathcal{O}^{\mathsf{PDec-Hon}}$  queries as follows. Whenever  $\mathcal{A}$  queries  $\mathcal{O}^{\mathsf{PDec-Hon}}$  on input  $(i, r_{\mathsf{Enc}})$ ,  $\mathcal{B}$  parses  $r_{\mathsf{Enc}}$  as  $(r_{\mathsf{Enc}}^{(1)}, \ldots, r_{\mathsf{Enc}}^{(K)})$ . Let  $j \in [K]$  such that party  $i \in B_j$ .

- If  $j \neq u$ ,  $\mathcal{B}$  computes  $(k,c) \leftarrow \Pi.\mathsf{Enc}(\mathsf{pk}_j; r_{\mathsf{Enc}}^{(j)})$  and returns  $d_i \leftarrow \Pi.\mathsf{PDec}(\mathsf{sk}_i, c)$ .
- If j = u,  $\mathcal{B}$  queries its own challenger's  $\mathcal{O}^{\mathsf{PDec\text{-}Hon}}$  oracle on input  $(i, r_{\mathsf{Enc}}^{(j)})$  and forwards the result to  $\mathcal{A}$ .

As a result,  $\mathcal{B}$  receives a decoder D and the set  $\mathcal{I}_{pd}$ . Next,  $\mathcal{B}$  constructs the decoder  $D_u$  as prescribed by the Trace algorithm of  $\Pi'$ . To do so,  $\mathcal{B}$  performs the test on the decoder D, and outputs a dummy decoder if the test fails.  $\mathcal{B}$  simulates the test as follows: If  $\rho' > 0$ ,  $\mathcal{B}$  needs to generate partial decryptions on behalf of  $\mathcal{I}_{pd}$  for the ciphertexts used in the test. For all  $j \neq u$ ,  $\mathcal{B}$  can trivially generate partial decryptions on behalf of parties in  $\mathcal{I}_{pd}^{(j)}$ , since the reduction knows all secret keys except for the challenge instance u. To simulate partial decryptions on behalf of parties in  $\mathcal{I}_{pd}^{(u)}$ ,  $\mathcal{B}$  makes use of the  $\mathcal{O}^{\mathsf{PDec-Hon}}$  oracle provided by its challenger as described above for the simulation of  $\mathcal{O}^{\mathsf{PDec-Hon}}$ . This is possible because  $\mathcal{B}$  knows the randomness  $r_{\mathsf{Enc}}$  for all ciphertexts it generates to test the decoder.

Then,  $\mathcal{B}$  submits  $D_u$  and  $\mathcal{I}_{pd}^{(u)}$  to its challenger. Denote with  $\mathsf{GoodTr}_{\mathcal{B}}$ ,  $\mathsf{BadTr}_{\mathcal{B}}$ , and  $\mathsf{GoodDec}_{\mathcal{B}}$  the events  $\mathsf{GoodTr}$ ,  $\mathsf{BadTr}$ , and  $\mathsf{GoodDec}$  for  $\mathcal{B}$  when running in the  $\tau$ -traceability game of  $\Pi$  against  $\rho$  partial insiders.

Before we bound  $\mathcal{A}$ 's probability to distinguish adjacent hybrids with  $\mathcal{B}$ 's success probability, we first prove the following intuitive claim, which says that a decoder  $D_u$  constructed from a decoder D that tested positive is good with overwhelming probability.

{28}------------------------------------------------

<span id="page-28-0"></span>Claim 6.7 For all adversaries  $\mathcal{A}$  and for all  $j \in [K]$  there exists a negligible function  $negl(\lambda)$  such that

$$\Pr\Bigl[\mathsf{test}_{\mathcal{A}} = 1 \wedge |\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}}{}^{(j)}| \leq \rho\Bigr] \leq \Pr\bigl[\mathsf{GoodDec}_{\mathcal{B}} \mid \mathcal{B}.u = j\bigr] + \mathsf{negl}(\lambda).$$

Proof of Claim 6.7. Suppose that  $|\mathcal{I}_{pd}^{(j)}| \leq \rho$ , and thus  $\mathcal{B}$  does not hit the abort condition to output a dummy decoder. Suppose that test happens. We will show that, in this case,  $\mathcal{B}$  produces a good decoder with overwhelming probability or in other words  $\Pr[\text{test}_{\mathcal{A}} = 1 \land D_u \text{ is not } \varepsilon/4\text{-good}] \leq \Pr[\text{test}_{\mathcal{A}} = 1 \mid D_u \text{ is not } \varepsilon/4\text{-good}] \leq \Pr[\lambda]$ . Denote with X the random variable counting the successful responses of D in the test. We can apply Lemma 6.5 and bound

$$\Pr\left[\text{test} = 1 | P(D_u) < \frac{1}{2} + \frac{\varepsilon}{4}\right] = \Pr\left[\text{test} = 1 | P(D) < \frac{1}{2} + \frac{\varepsilon}{4}\right]$$

$$\leq \Pr\left[\text{test} = 1 | P(D) = \frac{1}{2} + \frac{\varepsilon}{4}\right]$$

$$= \Pr\left[X \geq N \cdot \frac{1}{2} + \frac{\varepsilon}{2} | P(D) = \frac{1}{2} + \frac{\varepsilon}{4}\right],$$

where N denotes the number of repetitions in the test. Observe that, if  $P(D) = 1/2 + \varepsilon/4$ , then  $\mu := \mathbb{E}[X] = Q \cdot (1/2 + \varepsilon/4)$ , and let  $t = Q\varepsilon/4$ . We can apply Hoeffding's inequality and bound

$$\Pr\left[\mathsf{test} = 1 | P(D_u) < \frac{1}{2} + \frac{\varepsilon}{4}\right] \le \Pr[X \ge \mu + t] \le \exp\left(-\frac{Q\varepsilon^2}{8}\right),$$

which is negligible for  $Q \geq 8\lambda/\varepsilon^2$ . Since we set  $Q := 8\lambda/\varepsilon^2$  in the construction, the claim holds.

Equipped with Claim 6.7, we next bound  $\mathcal{A}$ 's advantage in distinguishing subsequent hybrids with respect to GoodTr and BadTr.

<span id="page-28-1"></span>**Claim 6.8** For all  $j \in [K]$  there exists a negligible function negl such that

$$\Pr\!\left[\mathsf{GoodTr}_{\mathcal{A}}^{(j)}\right] - \Pr\!\left[\mathsf{GoodTr}_{\mathcal{A}}^{(j-1)}\right] \leq \Pr\!\left[\mathsf{GoodDec}_{\mathcal{B}} \mid \mathcal{B}.u = j\right] - \Pr\!\left[\mathsf{GoodTr}_{\mathcal{B}} \mid \mathcal{B}.u = j\right] + \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$$

as well as

$$\Pr\Big[\mathsf{BadTr}_{\mathcal{A}}^{(j-1)}\Big] - \Pr\Big[\mathsf{BadTr}_{\mathcal{A}}^{(j)}] = \Pr[\mathsf{BadTr}_{\mathcal{B}} \mid \mathcal{B}.u = j\Big].$$

Proof of Claim 6.8. We start with the latter part of the claim. Observe that the only way for  $\mathcal{A}$  to set  $\mathsf{BadTr} = 1$  in  $\mathcal{H}_{j-1}$  but not in  $\mathcal{H}_j$  is to cause  $\mathsf{BadTrBin}_j = 1$ , i.e., causing the tracing procedure to output some  $\mathcal{T}'_j$  such that  $\mathcal{T}'_j \not\subseteq \mathcal{T}_j$ . Denote with  $\mathcal{T}'_{j,\mathcal{A}}$  and  $\mathcal{T}_{j,\mathcal{A}}$  the random variable describing the set of identified traitors in  $B_j$  and the set of real traitors from  $B_j$ , respectively, when  $\mathcal{A}$  runs in the tracing experiment of  $\Pi'$ . Similarly, denote with  $\mathcal{T}'_{j,\mathcal{B}}$  and  $\mathcal{T}_{j,\mathcal{B}}$  the same variables, when  $\mathcal{B}$  runs in the tracing experiment of  $\Pi$ . Applying the observation above, we can impose the following bound:

$$\Pr \Big[ \mathsf{BadTr}_{\mathcal{A}}^{(j-1)} \Big] - \Pr \Big[ \mathsf{BadTr}_{\mathcal{A}}^{(j)} \Big] = \Pr \Big[ \mathcal{T}_{j,\mathcal{A}}' \not\subseteq \mathcal{T}_{j,\mathcal{A}} \Big].$$

By construction of  $\Pi'$ . Trace and  $\mathcal{B}$ , it must also hold that

$$\Pr[\mathsf{BadTr}_{\mathcal{B}} \mid \mathcal{B}.u = j] = \Pr[\mathcal{T}'_{j,\mathcal{B}} \not\subseteq \mathcal{T}_{j,\mathcal{B}} \mid \mathcal{B}.u = j] = \Pr[\mathcal{T}'_{j,\mathcal{A}} \not\subseteq \mathcal{T}_{j,\mathcal{A}}],$$

and thus

$$\Pr \Big[ \mathsf{BadTr}_{\mathcal{A}}^{(j-1)} \Big] - \Pr \Big[ \mathsf{BadTr}_{\mathcal{A}}^{(j)} \Big] = \Pr [ \mathsf{BadTr}_{\mathcal{B}} \mid \mathcal{B}.u = j].$$

Next, we apply a similar argument to the first part of the claim. Again, the only way that  $\mathsf{GoodTr}_{\mathcal{A}}^{(j)} = 1$ , but  $\mathsf{GoodTr}_{\mathcal{A}}^{(j-1)} = 0$  is if  $\mathcal{A}$  has hit the modified condition in  $\mathcal{H}_j$ , i.e.,  $\mathsf{GoodTrBin}_j = 0$ ,  $|\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}}^{(j)}| \leq \rho$ , and  $\mathsf{test} = 1$ . Applying the law of total probability, we get that

$$\begin{split} \Pr\Big[\mathsf{GoodTr}_{\mathcal{A}}^{(j)}\Big] - \Pr\Big[\mathsf{GoodTr}_{\mathcal{A}}^{(j-1)}\Big] &\leq \Pr\Big[\neg \mathsf{GoodTrBin}_{j,\mathcal{A}} \wedge |\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}}^{(j)}| \leq \rho \wedge \mathsf{test}\Big] \\ &= \Pr\Big[\mathsf{test} \wedge |\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}}^{(j)}| \leq \rho\Big] - \Pr\Big[\mathsf{GoodTrBin}_{j,\mathcal{A}} \wedge |\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}}^{(j)}| \leq \rho \wedge \mathsf{test}\Big]. \end{split}$$

{29}------------------------------------------------

Again, by the law of total probability, this is equal to

$$\Pr \Big[ \mathsf{test} \wedge |\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}}{}^{(j)}| \leq \rho \Big] - \Pr \Big[ \mathsf{GoodTrBin}_{j,\mathcal{A}} \wedge |\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}}{}^{(j)}| \leq \rho \Big] + \Pr \Big[ \mathsf{GoodTrBin}_{j,\mathcal{A}} \wedge |\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}}{}^{(j)}| \leq \rho \wedge \mathsf{test} = 0 \Big]$$

Now, consider that, whenever test = 0, B outputs a dummy decoder. Hence, we get that

$$\begin{split} &\Pr\Big[\mathsf{test} \wedge |\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}}{}^{(j)}| \leq \rho\Big] - \Pr\Big[\mathsf{GoodTrBin}_{j,\mathcal{A}} \wedge |\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}}{}^{(j)}| \leq \rho\Big] + \Pr\Big[\mathsf{GoodTrBin}_{j,\mathcal{A}} \wedge |\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}}{}^{(j)}| \leq \rho \wedge \mathsf{test} = 0\Big] \\ &\leq \Pr\Big[\mathsf{test} \wedge |\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}}{}^{(j)}| \leq \rho\Big] - \Pr\Big[\mathsf{GoodTrBin}_{j,\mathcal{A}} \wedge |\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}}{}^{(j)}| \leq \rho\Big] + \Pr\big[\mathsf{GoodTrBin}_{j,\mathcal{A}} \mid \mathsf{test} = 0\Big] \\ &\leq \Pr\Big[\mathsf{test} \wedge |\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}}{}^{(j)}| \leq \rho\Big] - \Pr\Big[\mathsf{GoodTrBin}_{j,\mathcal{A}} \wedge |\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}}{}^{(j)}| \leq \rho\Big] + \Pr\Big[\Pi.\mathsf{Trace}^{\mathsf{Dummy}(\cdot)}(\mathsf{pk},\mathsf{tk},\varepsilon/4) \neq \emptyset\Big], \end{split}$$

where pk, tk, and Ipd are treated as random variables. Observe that due to the unframeability of Π, its tracing algorithm can never output a non-empty set of traitors when queried with the dummy decoder, except with negligible probability. It is easy to see that otherwise the trivial adversary who corrupts no one and outputs *D* = Dummy would have a non-negligible advantage against the traceability of Π. Hence, there exists a negligible function negl such that

$$\Pr \Big[ \Pi.\mathsf{Trace}^{\mathsf{Dummy}(\cdot)}(\mathsf{pk},\mathsf{tk},\varepsilon/4) \neq \emptyset \Big] \leq \mathsf{negl}(\lambda).$$

Applying additionally Claim [6.7](#page-28-0) to substitute Pr[test ∧ |Ipd (*j*) | ≤ *ρ*], and simplifying negligibilities yields the following:

$$\begin{split} &\Pr\!\left[\mathsf{GoodTr}_{\mathcal{A}}^{(j)}\right] - \Pr\!\left[\mathsf{GoodTr}_{\mathcal{A}}^{(j-1)}\right] \\ &\leq \Pr\!\left[\mathsf{GoodDec}_{\mathcal{B}}|\mathcal{B}.u = j\right] - \Pr\!\left[\mathsf{GoodTrBin}_{j,\mathcal{A}} \wedge |\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}}^{(j)}| \leq \rho\right] + \mathsf{negl}(\lambda) \\ &= \Pr\!\left[\mathsf{GoodDec}_{\mathcal{B}}|\mathcal{B}.u = j\right] - \Pr\!\left[\mathcal{T}_{\mathcal{B}}' \subseteq \mathcal{T}_{\mathcal{B}} \wedge |\mathcal{T}_{\mathcal{B}}| \geq \tau \wedge |\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}}^{(u)}| \leq \rho \mid \mathcal{B}.u = j\right] + \mathsf{negl}(\lambda) \\ &= \Pr\!\left[\mathsf{GoodDec}_{\mathcal{B}}|\mathcal{B}.u = j\right] - \Pr\!\left[\mathsf{GoodTr}_{j,\mathcal{B}} \mid \mathcal{B}.u = j\right] + \mathsf{negl}(\lambda). \end{split}$$

Making use of Claim [6.8,](#page-28-1) we get:

$$\begin{split} & \Pr \Big[ \mathsf{GoodTr}_{\mathcal{A}}^{(K)} \Big] - \Pr \Big[ \mathsf{GoodTr}_{\mathcal{A}}^{(0)} \Big] = \sum_{j=1}^{K} \Big( \Pr \Big[ \mathsf{GoodTr}_{\mathcal{A}}^{(j)} \Big] - \Pr \Big[ \mathsf{GoodTr}_{\mathcal{A}}^{(j-1)} \Big] \Big) \\ & \overset{\mathsf{Claim}}{\leq} \frac{6.8}{2} \sum_{j=1}^{K} \Big( \Pr [\mathsf{GoodDec}_{\mathcal{B}} \mid \mathcal{B}.u = j] - \Pr [\mathsf{GoodTr}_{\mathcal{B}} \mid \mathcal{B}.u = j] + \mathsf{negl}'(\lambda) \Big) \\ & = \sum_{j=1}^{K} \left( \frac{\Pr [\mathsf{GoodDec}_{\mathcal{B}} \wedge \mathcal{B}.u = j] - \Pr [\mathsf{GoodTr}_{\mathcal{B}} \wedge \mathcal{B}.u = j]}{\Pr [\mathcal{B}.u = j]} + \mathsf{negl}'(\lambda) \right) \\ & = K \cdot \sum_{j=1}^{K} \left( \Pr [\mathsf{GoodDec}_{\mathcal{B}} \wedge \mathcal{B}.u = j] - \Pr [\mathsf{GoodTr}_{\mathcal{B}} \wedge \mathcal{B}.u = j] \right) + \mathsf{negl}'(\lambda) \\ & = K \cdot \left( \Pr [\mathsf{GoodDec}_{\mathcal{B}}] - \Pr [\mathsf{GoodTr}_{\mathcal{B}}] \right) + K \cdot \mathsf{negl}'(\lambda) \\ & \leq K \cdot \mathsf{negl}(\lambda) \end{split}$$

for a negligible function negl, following traceability of Π. Hence, we get that

$$\begin{split} \Pr\Big[\mathsf{GoodTr}_{\mathcal{A}}^{(0)}\Big] & \geq \Pr\Big[\mathsf{GoodTr}_{\mathcal{A}}^{(K)}\Big] - K \cdot \mathsf{negl}(\lambda) \\ & \geq \Pr[\mathsf{GoodDec}_{\mathcal{A}}] - K \cdot \mathsf{negl}(\lambda). \end{split}$$

{30}------------------------------------------------

A similar argument applies to BadTr:

$$\begin{split} &\Pr\left[\mathsf{BadTr}_{\mathcal{A}}^{(0)}\right] - \Pr\left[\mathsf{BadTr}_{\mathcal{A}}^{(K)}\right] \\ &= \sum_{j=1}^{K} \left(\Pr\left[\mathsf{BadTr}_{\mathcal{A}}^{(j-1)}\right] - \Pr\left[\mathsf{BadTr}_{\mathcal{A}}^{(j)}\right]\right) \\ &\stackrel{\mathrm{Claim}}{=} \frac{6.8}{=} \sum_{j=1}^{K} \Pr[\mathsf{BadTr}_{\mathcal{B}} \mid \mathcal{B}.u = j] \\ &= \sum_{j=1}^{K} \frac{1}{\Pr[\mathcal{B}.u = j]} \Pr[\mathsf{BadTr}_{\mathcal{B}} \land \mathcal{B}.u = j] \\ &= K \cdot \sum_{j=1}^{K} \Pr[\mathsf{BadTr}_{\mathcal{B}} \land \mathcal{B}.u = j] \\ &= K \cdot \Pr[\mathsf{BadTr}_{\mathcal{B}}] \\ &\leq K \cdot \mathsf{negl}(\lambda), \end{split}$$

for a negligible function  $negl(\lambda)$ . Hence, we get that

$$\Pr \Big[ \mathsf{BadTr}_{\mathcal{A}}^{(0)} \Big] \ \leq \Pr \Big[ \mathsf{BadTr}_{\mathcal{A}}^{(K)} \Big] + K \cdot \mathsf{negl}(\lambda) = K \cdot \mathsf{negl}(\lambda).$$

# <span id="page-30-0"></span>7 Multi-Instance Expansion

In this section, we prove Theorem 2.5 as well as the robustness analysis leading to Corollary 2.6.

We start our analysis by showing that we can retain  $\tau$ -traceability against  $\rho$  partial insiders of a scheme  $\Pi$ , when encrypting using a 1-out-of- $\ell$  threshold across  $\ell$  instances, each instantiated with  $\Pi$ . Then, we show that applying this compiler to our 1-partition scheme allows us to make an improved robustness guarantee.

<span id="page-30-1"></span>Construction 4. Let  $\ell \in \mathsf{poly}(\lambda)$  and let  $\Pi$  be a  $\tau$ -traceable TT-KEM against  $\rho$  partial insiders. We construct  $\Pi'$  as follows:

 $\Pi'$ .KGen(1<sup>λ</sup>,  $n, f, t, \varepsilon$ ): Run  $\ell$  instances of  $\Pi$ .KGen:

$$\left\{\left(\mathsf{pk}^{(j)}, \{\mathsf{sk}_i^{(j)}\}_{i \in [n]}, \mathsf{tk}^{(j)}\right) \xleftarrow{\$} \Pi.\mathsf{KGen}(1^\lambda, n, r, t, \varepsilon/4\ell)\right\}_{j \in [\ell]}$$

Set 
$$\mathsf{pk} \coloneqq \{\mathsf{pk}^{(j)}\}_{j \in [\ell]}$$
,  $\mathsf{sk}_i \coloneqq \{\mathsf{sk}_i^{(j)}\}_{j \in [\ell]}$ , and  $\mathsf{tk} \coloneqq \{\mathsf{tk}^{(j)}\}_{j \in [\ell]}$ . Output  $(\mathsf{pk}, \{\mathsf{sk}_i\}_{i \in [n]}, \mathsf{tk})$ .

- Π'.Enc(pk): Sample a random KEM key  $k \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathcal{K}$ , and run encryption in every instance to generate  $(k_j, c_j) \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \Pi.$ Enc(pk<sup>(j)</sup>). Compute  $u_j \leftarrow k \oplus k_j$  for all  $j \in [\ell]$ . Finally, assemble  $c \coloneqq \{(c_j, u_j)\}_{j \in [\ell]}$  and output (k, c).
- $\Pi'.\mathsf{PDec}(\mathsf{sk}_i,c) \text{: Compute } d_i^{(j)} \leftarrow \Pi.\mathsf{PDec}(\mathsf{sk}_i^{(j)},c_j) \text{ for all instances } j \in [\ell] \text{ and output } d_i \coloneqq \{d_i^{(j)}\}_{j \in [\ell]}.$
- $\Pi'$ .Combine(pk, S,  $\{d_i\}_{i\in[n]}, c$ ): Given partial decryptions from a set of parties in S, verify that there exists an instance j such that S is sufficient to decrypt in j. Then compute  $k_j \leftarrow \Pi$ .Combine(S,  $\{d_i^{(j)}\}_{i\in S}, c_j$ ) for such j and output  $k \leftarrow k_j \oplus u_j$ .
- $\Pi'.\mathsf{Trace}^D(\mathsf{pk},\mathsf{tk},\varepsilon,\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}},\{\mathsf{sk}_i\}_{i\in\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}}})$ : For each  $j\in[\ell]$ , construct a decoder  $D_j$  for the j-th instance of  $\Pi$  and run  $\mathcal{T}'_j \overset{\hspace{0.1em}\mathsf{\scriptscriptstyle\$}}{\leftarrow} \Pi.\mathsf{Trace}^{D_j}(\mathsf{pk}^{(j)},\mathsf{tk}^{(j)},\varepsilon/4\ell,\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}},\{\mathsf{sk}_i^{(j)}\}_{i\in\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}}})$ . Finally, output  $\mathcal{T}'\leftarrow\bigcup_{j\in[\ell]}\mathcal{T}'_j$ . To do so, construct the decoder  $\mathcal{D}_j$  making use of D. In particular, on input  $(c_j,k_j,\{d_i^{(j)}\}_{i\in\mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}}})$ , do the following:

{31}------------------------------------------------

- <span id="page-31-2"></span>• For  $q \in [\ell] \setminus \{j\}$ , generate  $(c_q, k_q) \stackrel{\hspace{0.1em}\mathsf{\scriptscriptstyle\$}}{\leftarrow} \Pi.\mathsf{Enc}(\mathsf{pk}^{(q)})$  and compute  $d_i^{(q)} \leftarrow \Pi.\mathsf{PDec}(\mathsf{sk}_i^{(q)}, c_q)$  for all  $i \in \mathcal{I}_{\mathsf{pd}}$ .
- Sample  $k^0$  and  $k^1$  uniformly from  $\mathcal{K}$ , as well as a random bit  $b \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \{0,1\}$ .
- For q < j, sample  $u_q \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathcal{K}$ , for  $q \ge j$  (in particular, for q = j), set  $u_q \leftarrow k_q \oplus k^0$ .
- Assemble  $c \coloneqq \{(c_q, u_q)\}_{q \in [\ell]}$  and  $d_i \coloneqq \{d_i^{(q)}\}_{q \in [\ell]}$  for all  $i \in \mathcal{I}_{pd}$ . Output  $b \oplus D\left(c, k^b, \{d_i\}_{i \in \mathcal{I}_{pd}}\right)$ .

**Parameter Sizes:** If  $\Pi$  has ciphetext size C(n), public key size P(n), and secret key size S(n), then  $\Pi'$  has sizes  $C'(n) = \ell \cdot C(n)$ ,  $P'(n) = \ell \cdot P(n)$ , and  $S'(n) = \ell \cdot S(n)$ .

Note that this compiler has similarities with Zhandry's user expansion compiler [51], which allows for extending the number of users at the cost of increased ciphertext size in traceable broadcast encryption. In particular, our construction uses a similar PLBE-style technique to "revoke" instances linearly during tracing.

<span id="page-31-1"></span>**Theorem 7.1 (Formal Version of Theorem 2.5).** If  $\Pi$  is  $\tau$ -traceable against  $\rho$  partial insiders, then so is the multi-instance scheme  $\Pi'$ . Whenever  $\rho > 0$ , we require that  $\Pi$  offers a partial decryption oracle  $\mathcal{O}^{\mathsf{PDec\text{-}Hon}}$ . If  $\Pi$  offers a partial decryption oracle  $\mathcal{O}^{\mathsf{PDec\text{-}Hon}}$ , then so does  $\Pi'$ .

It is intuitive to see why traceability is retained: Regarding unframability (i.e.,  $\mathsf{BadTr}$ ), if a decoder manages to frame a non-traitor, then in at least one instance j, tracing must have returned a non-traitor on input  $D_j$ , hence a non-traitor has been framed in the base scheme  $\Pi$ . This can happen only with negligible probability due to unframability of  $\Pi$ . Similarly, if D is a good decoder, we can show that, à la PLBE, for at least one instance j, the constructed decoder  $D_j$  must also be a good decoder. As a result, the tracing in instance j on  $D_j$  will yield at least K real traitors.

The proof of Theorem 7.1 follows closely the proof of user's expansion compiler [51], and can be found in Appendix C.1.
